  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b8c19ab2-f97b-46ac-8482-cc137dac7add'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15615865292107735110">Electronic and dancing violinist Lindsey Stirling shares her unconventional journey in an inspiring memoir filled with the energy, persistence, and humor that have helped her successfully pursue a passion outside the box.<br/><br/>A classically trained musician gone rogue, Lindsey Stirling is the epitome of independent, millennial-defined success: after being voted off the set of <i>Am</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15615865292107735110" style="display:none">Electronic and dancing violinist Lindsey Stirling shares her unconventional journey in an inspiring memoir filled with the energy, persistence, and humor that have helped her successfully pursue a passion outside the box.<br /><br />A classically trained musician gone rogue, Lindsey Stirling is the epitome of independent, millennial-defined success: after being voted off the set of <i>America’s Got Talent</i>, she went on to amass more than ten million social media fans, record two full-length albums, release multiple hits with billions of YouTube views, and tour sold-out venues across the world.<br /><br />Lindsey is not afraid to be herself. In fact, it’s her confidence and individuality that have propelled her into the spotlight. But the road hasn’t been easy. After being rejected by talent scouts, music reps, and eventually national television, Lindsey forged her own path, step by step. Here, for the first time, she shares every triumph and trial she has faced until now. Beginning in a humble yet charmed childhood, this book follows Lindsey through a humorous adolescence, to her life as a struggling musician, through her personal struggles with anorexia, and finally all the way to her success as a world-class entertainer. Lindsey’s magnetizing story is at once remarkable and universal—a testimony that there is no singular recipe for success. And a witness that, despite what people may say, sometimes it’s okay to be <i>The Only Pirate at the Party</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15615865292107735110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

There are a co<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">All kids, parents, and families are different, but I can say I read this with my 11 year old daughter and we both enjoyed it very much. There are a couple of mildly adult themes we paused to talk about as we read, but they are pretty mild and that opportunity to talk is part of what I liked about the book.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3764791270258233363">3.5 stars. Lindsey's voice imitations hurt my ears, and her childhood stories made me roll my eyes, but this is undeniably insightful and honest. I especially enjoyed hearing her talk about how she developed her creative ideas.</span>

<div id="review_1801727007" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1801727007" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1801727007?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=mem-wars">mem-wars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=pop-goes-the-culture">pop-goes-the-culture</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1801727007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15933387677507122648"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>If you've been following me for a while, you know that I've tried several memoirs by YouTube celebrities and did not like any of them. If you haven't been following me for a while, you're probably rolling your eyes a little and thinking, "Then why are you reading this, huh? Didn't you learn your lesson the last three times?" In response to this question: 1) No. And 2) What's a lesson?<br/><br/><br/><br/>I've actually been listening to Lindsey's music for on</span>
  <span id="freeText15933387677507122648" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>If you've been following me for a while, you know that I've tried several memoirs by YouTube celebrities and did not like any of them. If you haven't been following me for a while, you're probably rolling your eyes a little and thinking, "Then why are you reading this, huh? Didn't you learn your lesson the last three times?" In response to this question: 1) No. And 2) What's a lesson?<br><br><br><br>I've actually been listening to Lindsey's music for only about a year (late in the game, I know). I wish I could say that it was an independent discovery, but I don't even have that claim to fame. Someone I know likes her music a lot, so I got them her two CDs as a gift. Curious, I played a few of her songs on YouTube and was blown away - by the music, the crossing of genres, the talent, the dancing, the energy, the <i>outfits</i>.<br><br><br><br>My favorite songs by her are probably Senbonzakura, which is a cover of a Vocaloid song; Master of Tides, which is an incredible live performance with a nautical theme; and Minimal Beat, which is pretty much what it sounds like, paired with a montage of Lindsey on tour, greeting her fans in a multitude of countries in a multitude of outfits. If it sounds like I'm hung up on the outfits, that's because I am. Her fashion sense = life goals.<br><br><br><br>But it sucks learning the dirt on your favorite celebrities because sometimes when you peek into their closets you find not just skeletons but <i>meanness</i>. Nothing is worse than finding out a celebrity you love and adore is actually <i>not a nice person</i>. So that was a definite fear of mine when I was debating on reading THE ONLY PIRATE AT THE PARTY. But then her memoir got nominated for a Goodreads Choice Award, so I bit the bullet and checked it out from the library.<br><br><br><br>I really shouldn't have doubted.<br><br><br><br>Not because this memoir sucked, but because it was so awesome. Shame on me for thinking that somebody with so much talent, passion, energy, and intelligence wouldn't be able to string to words together. I finished THE ONLY PIRATE AT THE PARTY in a day, basically. Lindsey talks about her unconventional childhood, her Mormon faith (which actually causes some pretty sticky restraints on her wardrobe - that poor stylist, haha), her road to stardom, and her struggle with anxiety and eating disorders. She was charming and real, and just awkward enough to make you feel like you were actually reading somebody's private journal, and hearing their inner-most thoughts.<br><br><br><br>It really made me appreciate how difficult it is to achieve fame when you're starting out from nothing. I know most celebrity memoirs make that claim, but Lindsey shared some of her humiliations, like being shunned by a famous singer and his orchestra at a concert they were performing at together, and her rejection from the judges of <i>America's Got Talent</i>. I found it inspiring how she always tried to look for the silver lining in even the worst situations, and kept looking for new opportunities.<br><br><br><br>Honestly, I haven't been this psyched about a memoir since Mara Wilson's and Felicia Day's.<br><br><br><br>4.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="15933387677507122648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1817303857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13742314095169060814">i love how we get some humor in the book but also get some bittersweet feelings. <br/>overall rating: 4.9/5<br/><br/><br/><b>reread on may 3, 2017</b><br/><br/>i'll just put this out there- i'm a lindsey stirling fan, yes. am i a total fangirl and enthusiast? no. but i tried not to get my opinions on her to muddle up with my feelings on the book. <br/><br/><i>“Life is kind, and full of great moments, but I think the greatest moment of my life is always ahead of me. When I reach it, there will be another, greater moment to come.” </i><br/><br/>i don't usually</span>
  <span id="freeText13742314095169060814" style="display:none">i love how we get some humor in the book but also get some bittersweet feelings. <br />overall rating: 4.9/5<br /><br /><br /><b>reread on may 3, 2017</b><br /><br />i'll just put this out there- i'm a lindsey stirling fan, yes. am i a total fangirl and enthusiast? no. but i tried not to get my opinions on her to muddle up with my feelings on the book. <br /><br /><i>“Life is kind, and full of great moments, but I think the greatest moment of my life is always ahead of me. When I reach it, there will be another, greater moment to come.” </i><br /><br />i don't usually read autobiography/memoirs, and when i do, i usually lose interest in them. now i don't know if it's my head or my heart speaking, but lindsey stirling grasped me. she didn't obscure the mistakes she made. she opened up on them, and that's one thing i admire about a good memoir. they open up, and not everything is sunshine and rainbows. they don't just open the good things. they include all personalities, the ugly things, the pretty thing, the selfish things, the insecure things, no matter what the response. i don't like memoirs. but this one, lindsey stirling, beckoned me like a little voice saying 'let's jump on this book. it's good', and it was correct. there was a lot of humor incorporated in this book, and that made me chuckle (when i wasn't supposed to talk during testing) and made me extremely happy to read.<br /><br /><i><br />“My evolution as a violinist has included many thrilling performances, and I still love what I do, but there are times when even I get burned out. When this happens, I go back to that moment ten years ago. I picture myself on the stage with my bow in the air. I feel my heart racing, I see the faces in the audience smiling, and I remember the moment I thought, "I have to make this my life.” </i><br /><br />usually, when i read memoirs and throw them in the dnf trash bin, it's because when the person that you admire and look up to opens up about their personality, you find out that they <i>are actually a mean person</i>. i've had my doubts about reading this book because i always have thrown memoirs in the dnf because i just don't enjoy them.<br /><br />surprisingly enough, i flew through the only pirate at the party. i read it during lunch. i read it during class. i loved it. and lindsey stirling, you should be proud. because you are a true human bean and amazing and lovable and omg your music is amazing.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5797052227165692896">Lindsey Stirling is a dancing electronic violinist who first came to national attention as a result of her appearances on America's Got Talent. I remember thinking that she was incredibly talented, and I was shocked like everyone else when she was eliminated. This was all I knew about her before I picked up this book. I wouldn't have even call myself a fan of her music simply because I don't want to take anything away from her hard-core Stirlingites. Then why did I pick up the book you may ask? </span>
  <span id="freeText5797052227165692896" style="display:none">Lindsey Stirling is a dancing electronic violinist who first came to national attention as a result of her appearances on America's Got Talent. I remember thinking that she was incredibly talented, and I was shocked like everyone else when she was eliminated. This was all I knew about her before I picked up this book. I wouldn't have even call myself a fan of her music simply because I don't want to take anything away from her hard-core Stirlingites. Then why did I pick up the book you may ask? She's always seemed like the girl next door with the quirky sense of humor, The kind of person that everyone wants to be friends with (plus she's wearing a pirate costume on the cover, who doesn't want to be friends with someone like that) <br /><br />My favorite audiobooks are the ones where celebrity authors make it feel like they're having a conversation with you. Lindsey delivers that here.<br /><br />Lindsey, you no longer have to be the only pirate at the party, I'm always available ;)<br /></span>

<div id="review_1799936937" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1799936937" />
    <a title="Erica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2644090-erica"><img alt="Erica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558548351p2/2644090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1799936937?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica" href="/user/show/2644090-erica">Erica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781442393677" href="/book/show/25409725-the-only-pirate-at-the-party">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=sisters">sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=adorable">adorable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=biographical">biographical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=women-and-girls">women-and-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=growing-up">growing-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=famous-figures">famous-figures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=girlfriend-power">girlfriend-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=inspiring">inspiring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2644090-erica?shelf=travel">travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799936937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8145768880451336415">Am I the only one who thought, "Willow plays violin?" upon first-ever seeing Lindsey Stirling?<br/><br/>I'm going to tell you, straight up, that if you're turned off by upbeat Pollyanna-ism and stormclouds that have the sparkliest of silver linings, you're probably not going to enjoy this biography. If those things don't bother you, though, and if you enjoy reading about people's lives, especially about spunky musicians, I strongly recommend this!<br/><br/>In full cattiness, I can't say that I know whether or not t</span>
  <span id="freeText8145768880451336415" style="display:none">Am I the only one who thought, "Willow plays violin?" upon first-ever seeing Lindsey Stirling?<br /><br />I'm going to tell you, straight up, that if you're turned off by upbeat Pollyanna-ism and stormclouds that have the sparkliest of silver linings, you're probably not going to enjoy this biography. If those things don't bother you, though, and if you enjoy reading about people's lives, especially about spunky musicians, I strongly recommend this!<br /><br />In full cattiness, I can't say that I know whether or not this memoir is representative of Stirling's true personality, it may be the result of her PR team making her sound like a precocious Disney youth from the '50's. However, genuine or not, I enjoyed Stirling's happy attitude, her dorky stories, and her ability to point out and laugh at/bemoan her own flaws. She comes across as sharply self-aware, down-to-earth, positive, and driven. She admits her downfalls and defeats gracefully and with a touch of shame but not so much that it sounds like she dwells on the darker moments of her life. And she's catty, too! Not mean, but she calls out bad or ridiculous behavior that she's encountered and while she does so with a lighthearted touch, there's a bit of tooth in those tellings.<br /><br />I was surprised to relate to so many of her tales. While I have no musical talent at all, nor do I dance, nor am I a YouTuber, nor am I Mormon, nor have I ever had an eating disorder, nor does anyone ask for my autograph or for pictures when I'm out and about, I <i>did</i> grow up in a frugal household (that's code for "poor"), I have hilarious sibling stories, I have control issues, I travel in comfy clothes unless I have to look good the moment I arrive at my destination, I also do crazy lady things (exercising in the airport), I also feel down pillows are horrible traps of unsupportiveness; I don’t like Nutella; I believe expiration dates are just reminders to smell your food before you use it; and I firmly believe unevenly-spread peanut butter is evil.<br />And her car! Me, too! I cannot let go of my car! It was the first one I ever bought all by myself and we've traveled a lot of this country together. It's got 220K miles, a broken windshield that I really need to replace, problems galore, weird little idiosyncrasies, and it's probably not really safe to drive. When it last broke down a year ago, I had to buy a new (used and cheap) car and I should have traded mine in but I couldn't. My brother bought it off me, instead, and when I got the money, I bought it back and he and I been working on it together, trying to get it back in running condition because I just cannot give it up while it may still have some life.<br />I wasn't too generationally removed from Stirling, either, thanks to the crowd I currently hang with; they're all her age. I admit, though, I was surprised to find she's 30 and not 22. I'd never bothered to stalk her, I just assumed she was really young. She's small and she looks just-post-pubescent; it sounds like this is a common misperception.<br />So, yeah. I connected with this bubbly, silly, driven, charming entertainer despite having little in common with her. It was just so hard not to!<br /><br />She reads the audio version, which is delightful. At first, it's not. At first, she's nervous and she sounds like that student who is called upon to read out loud but who doesn't hear or comprehend the words coming out of her mouth. She warms up to her story pretty quickly, though.<br />I'm a little sad her sister, who is credited as co-author, wasn't a co-reader, as well. I can only imagine how much fun they'd have had in the studio together.<br /><br />As an aside, I had noticed and wondered why she sounded all choked-up when she introduced and talked about about Gavi. It seemed so over the top and sentimental, like she was the kind of person who cries at commercials about kittens or who gets verklempt when she thinks of something nice someone did for her one time.<br />Then, at the very end, after the book is done, there’s an <a href="http://www.altpress.com/news/entry/jason_gaviati" rel="nofollow noopener">In Memorium</a> that she cries through and my heart broke. Reading those parts of the book must have been so hard and bittersweet. Ouch.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8145768880451336415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Stirling fans, music fans, America's got Talent alumni</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62220551-r-f-gammon?shelf=faves-2016">faves-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62220551-r-f-gammon?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62220551-r-f-gammon?shelf=humor">humor</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846651083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16102014530495631792">I am a huge Lindsey Stirling fan, although I only discovered her a couple of weeks ago. I read this book in one sitting and it was AMAZING. The strength within her is so amazing. She is so counter-cultural, so different from so many people. She overcame her eating disorder, took overwhelming criticism on America's Got Talent and from many other people, and survived the loss and gain of friends and siblings, and she is an incredibly strong young woman. I can honestly say that I want to be like Li</span>
  <span id="freeText16102014530495631792" style="display:none">I am a huge Lindsey Stirling fan, although I only discovered her a couple of weeks ago. I read this book in one sitting and it was AMAZING. The strength within her is so amazing. She is so counter-cultural, so different from so many people. She overcame her eating disorder, took overwhelming criticism on America's Got Talent and from many other people, and survived the loss and gain of friends and siblings, and she is an incredibly strong young woman. I can honestly say that I want to be like Lindsey when I grow up - not because she's famous, but because her character is an amazing testimony to her values and her faith.</span>

<div id="review_2454019040" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2454019040" />
    <a title="Mikayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14064833-mikayla"><img alt="Mikayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506697152p2/14064833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2454019040?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2018</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16927710067598432870">I read this in one evening (I'm telling you, library duedates do wonders for reading). I'm honestly not quite what I expected, but a laugh-out-loud-then-almost-cry kind of book was not it. I loved Lindsey's light writing style, though she was unafraid to talk abut deeper things. <br/>I loved the honesty displyed in this book, and how she talked honestly about her faith, without being pushy. Her abition to be modest dispite Hollywood's constant push that she be otherwise is really cool.<br/>Her dedication </span>
  <span id="freeText16927710067598432870" style="display:none">I read this in one evening (I'm telling you, library duedates do wonders for reading). I'm honestly not quite what I expected, but a laugh-out-loud-then-almost-cry kind of book was not it. I loved Lindsey's light writing style, though she was unafraid to talk abut deeper things. <br />I loved the honesty displyed in this book, and how she talked honestly about her faith, without being pushy. Her abition to be modest dispite Hollywood's constant push that she be otherwise is really cool.<br />Her dedication to her work and her fight aginst anerexia was inspiring. <br /><br />There were a couple of refrances to undressed people, but only when telling fairly innoecent stories. I would be completly comfortable handing this book to a tweleve year old, dispite a couple embarresing stories. </span>

<div id="review_1514863543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1514863543" />
    <a title="Classics Lover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51657295-classics-lover"><img alt="Classics Lover" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1514863543?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Classics Lover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Classics Lover" href="/user/show/51657295-classics-lover">Classics Lover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everybody</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1514863543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17009268453208023542">"Asking a working writer what he (or she) thinks about critics is like asking a lamp-post what it thinks about dogs." Christopher Hampton - British playwright<br/><br/>I, however, shall invoke the wisdom found in the old Chinese Proverb: "Do not use a hatchet to remove a fly from your friend's forehead."<br/><br/>Some have asked:"What could possibly motivate Lindsey Stirling to write a memoir at the ripe old age of 29?"<br/><br/>As I read her book (co-written by the lovely and talented Brooke S. Passey) I discovered several </span>
  <span id="freeText17009268453208023542" style="display:none">"Asking a working writer what he (or she) thinks about critics is like asking a lamp-post what it thinks about dogs." Christopher Hampton - British playwright<br /><br />I, however, shall invoke the wisdom found in the old Chinese Proverb: "Do not use a hatchet to remove a fly from your friend's forehead."<br /><br />Some have asked:"What could possibly motivate Lindsey Stirling to write a memoir at the ripe old age of 29?"<br /><br />As I read her book (co-written by the lovely and talented Brooke S. Passey) I discovered several reasons.<br /><br />An obvious reason needs a bit of backstory: Those who have had dealings in the publishing world know that it has its own orbit around the sun. Scientific calculations place it, time-wise, somewhere between the orbit of Halley's Comet and that of Pluto. The result being that when someone FROM that publishing world says..."A month...at most." One has to understand that THEIR month is not a normal Earth-time month.<br /> <br />Lindsey Stirling ALSO has her own orbit around the sun...but it is FASTER than everybody else's.<br /><br />"Lindsey Time" (besides being the name of her secondary Youtube Channel - because apparently the time, energy, and effort in creating content for ONLY one Youtube Channel was too wussy) ALSO explains why she gets more done in a day then the rest of us mere mortals, who are just (comparatively) standing-still...perhaps daydreaming about getting rich recycling bellybutton lint, or wondering why nobody ever invented a DVD re-winder.<br /><br />So, just this past year besides producing/designing all of the content for the aforementioned two Youtube channels, she also designed a tour. And by design I mean just that.<br /><br />Besides previously having written the music, she did the idea sketches for the costumes, she did power-points for the set designs, implemented new technology so her song performances evoked the experience of the videos, only live versions. SO elaborate. She also gave the choreographer her visions for the new dancers and herself. This girl KNOWS what she wants and is involved in EVERY aspect. <br /><br />Lindsey attended many award ceremonies, performed in television specials, and in her spare time finished a book.<br /><br />AND...<br /><br />This is Lindsey "slowing down". She actually gets a WHOLE six hours of sleep a night now. Tacking on a whole two more hours from her previous four hour a night nap.<br /><br />JUST like BRUCE LEE! (Yes. That IS a subtle reference to her latest music video "HEIST";) <br /><br />(PLUS, She has a wicked strong broom-tossing arm. The police could utilize her skill in raids.)<br /><br />All the evidence shows this Lady has done a lot of amazing things. Already.<br /><br />If she had waited any longer, Brooke would have had to echo Herman Melville: "Give me a condor's quill! Give me Vesuvius' crater for an inkstand!" <br /><br />The question should not be "Why would Lindsey Stirling write a memoir already?" but "Why is this not required reading?" <br /><br />EVERYBODY can learn something from this book. <br /><br />Sure...there ARE guys out there that communicate by word or deed that they don't believe girls are very smart. Let me break the "Guy Code" here: Guys see the type of "genuine doughheads", putzes, and utterly repulsive players that girls swoon over. Simply because they are quote-unquote "cute". Even the guys who ARE the genuine doughheads/putzes/utterly repulsive players cannot believe girls fall for their line either. <br /><br />Enter the Dragon...uh...Lindsey Stirling.<br /><br />Quoting from pages 118 -119: Speaking of "John Doe" - "He was charming, muscular, and had a smile that would melt your face off." Further - "...he was smoother than a greased cookie sheet. On the flip side, the man was also as deep as a greased cookie sheet."<br /><br />"...everyone I knew fell in love with him, except for me."<br /><br />Let the bells ring out and the sky turn blue!<br /><br />Hope blossoms in the world again!<br /><br />Not only is Lindsey Stirling not easily conned, but she is intelligent, determined, focused, relentless, passionate, invigorated (and invigorating) talented, accomplished... <br /><br />...and my hero. <br /><br />She reminds me of Caleb, in the Old Testament. The Anakims, the giants, were still inhabiting the promised land, and they had to be overcome. Said Caleb, now at 85 years of age: “Give me this mountain” Josh. 14:12<br /><br />In other words: Give me these challenges.<br /><br />That's Lindsey Stirling.<br /><br />Quoting British literary critic George Saintsbury: "Criticism is the endeavor to find, to know, to love, to recommend, not only the best, but all the good, that has been known and thought and written in the world."<br /><br />With that said, I highly recommend Lindsey Stirling's memoir: The Only Pirate At The Party. <br /><br />Darwin<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17009268453208023542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1471435768" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471435768" />
    <a title="Adrianna [SypherLily]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2997955-adrianna-sypherlily"><img alt="Adrianna [SypherLily]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399076174p2/2997955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1471435768?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adrianna [SypherLily]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adrianna [SypherLily]" href="/user/show/2997955-adrianna-sypherlily">Adrianna [SypherLily]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2997955-adrianna-sypherlily?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471435768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12535252592646659329">Lindsey Stirling is a dancing violinist who brings joy and positivity wherever she goes. She's extremely talented, and a breath of fresh air when it comes to celebrities, even if she's not of that status yet. She's utterly humble, thoughtful of others, and always trying her best to stay grounded and stick to her morals and religious beliefs. <br/><br/>While I'm not Mormon, I can truly respect the lengths she goes to to make sure she's surrounded by those who follow her rules (such as no drinking/drugs/sex</span>
  <span id="freeText12535252592646659329" style="display:none">Lindsey Stirling is a dancing violinist who brings joy and positivity wherever she goes. She's extremely talented, and a breath of fresh air when it comes to celebrities, even if she's not of that status yet. She's utterly humble, thoughtful of others, and always trying her best to stay grounded and stick to her morals and religious beliefs. <br /><br />While I'm not Mormon, I can truly respect the lengths she goes to to make sure she's surrounded by those who follow her rules (such as no drinking/drugs/sex on her bus), and also to be sure she stays modest with her wardrobe, both performing, and during interviews or parties. <br /><br />In her autobiography she talks of her upbringing, how she's still learning to love herself, her battle with an eating disorder, her hard work she has to put toward her career, how she deals with everyday life, and gives us cute, funny, meaningful, and even sad stories from her life. <br /><br />If you're listening to the audiobook, I'll warn you the first 23 chapters she sounds like someone reading aloud in school from a textbook. When she hits chapter 24, she seems to be comfortable and actually sounds lively and like herself. And when she starts to speak about her best friend Gavi, you'll hear her voice quivering, even as she speaks of him in the present. But Gavi had passed before this book was published, and you can hear the pain and tears in her voice every time she speaks of him. <br /><br />I've been a fan of Lindsey's music since she posted her Electric Daisy video, which alongside Spontaneous Me, are still my favorites of her original tracks. I've been in the front line by the stage of her concert, had her sign a poster, and also got a hug. I've watched so many videos of hers, along with Gavi and the rest of her crew, that I feel like I'm watching family. <br /><br />If you don't know anything about this girl before you read this book, I don't think you'll enjoy it much. She's bubbly and goofy, talented and driven, but it's not a funny memoir or an autobiography about someone who did major world changing events. <br /><br />It's about a girl who loves to dance and play her violin. A girl who wants to make anyone who sees or listens to her feel happy. A girl who tells you to follow your dream no matter how big, because if you work hard, you can get there. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12535252592646659329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2627006057585756248">I've loved Lindsey's music, but I appreciate it a lot more after reading her book. I found myself learning from her, and by the end she felt like a friend. In the unfortunate and tragic event that I would ever become famous, I hope I would be as indifferent and unaffected by it as Lindsey is. Her normalcy is refreshing. (Also, her book made me feel less like I'm the only pirate at the party.)</span>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12199278471433262381">I am a little biased but I am a stirlingite by heart, I'm sorry. But it's true, which is why when I saw this book at the store, I immediately picked it up, Lindsey and her sister both write this book in such a way, that Lindsey is basically talking to you. I also listened to Lindsey's albums when I was reading this to get in depth with her music.   <span id="freeText12199278471433262381" style="display:none">I am a little biased but I am a stirlingite by heart, I'm sorry. But it's true, which is why when I saw this book at the store, I immediately picked it up, Lindsey and her sister both write this book in such a way, that Lindsey is basically talking to you. I also listened to Lindsey's albums when I was reading this to get in depth with her music. I got to understand my hero on a more human level, since sometimes we picture our heroes as gods. <br /><br />Lindsey takes us on a journey through her personal struggles along with funny stories and what she is like as a person, i see Lindsey as opening up to her fans, like REALLY going in depth and I respect that, it's a love letter to us as well the fans, giving us insight on her tour as well the music business in general. Something that I am sooooo interested about. So as a huge fan this book is really good. Heck I finished it in four days! I rarely do that, let alone write a review. <br /><br />I honestly hope they write another one, for she is a rising star who has not even hit the tip of the iceberg yet, I just hope I can be there when she does </span>

<div id="review_1510024940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510024940" />
    <a title="Taryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13977687-taryn"><img alt="Taryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591322913p2/13977687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510024940?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taryn" href="/user/show/13977687-taryn">Taryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781442393677" href="/book/show/25409725-the-only-pirate-at-the-party">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13977687-taryn?shelf=2016-release">2016-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510024940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4655952591041880599">I snapped up an audio version of this book because I've long been a fan of electric violinist Lindsey Stirling's music videos on YouTube. If you're not familiar with her particular brand of art, picture a tiny redhead dancing around like a pixie in exotic locales, all while furiously bowing a stringed instrument—and sometimes dressed up as a video game character.<br/><br/>(Can I just take a moment to say how much I love the way the internet has opened up avenues for people a touch outside the mainstream? </span>
  <span id="freeText4655952591041880599" style="display:none">I snapped up an audio version of this book because I've long been a fan of electric violinist Lindsey Stirling's music videos on YouTube. If you're not familiar with her particular brand of art, picture a tiny redhead dancing around like a pixie in exotic locales, all while furiously bowing a stringed instrument—and sometimes dressed up as a video game character.<br /><br />(Can I just take a moment to say how much I love the way the internet has opened up avenues for people a touch outside the mainstream? Stirling was famously slammed by the judges on America's Got Talent, but on YouTube she was able to find people who “get” her and her music—and there are a lot of them. I love hearing the success stories of people who pursue what they're good at, even if not everyone understands it.)<br /><br />Because I find Stirling's professional life so interesting—what is life like for a YouTuber and touring musician, really?—I was surprised to find my favorite parts of the book focused on her childhood, family, and regular life outside of music. She still drives a 2002 Toyota Echo even though she can afford something a little flashier because, as she points out, the car she's had since college still works (and if it ain't broke...). I can totally respect that kind of frugality. <br /><br />Less endearing were the sections in which she discussed her fame and some of the negative effects it's had on her life. While I understand that fans can be pushy and entitled and touring can be exhausting, I don't have much patience for celebrities who publicly complain about such things. Those are issues to vent about to family members and close friends, not the people who provide the funds that make your lifestyle possible (I mean, they did just fork over the cash to buy your book, after all).<br /><br />More book recommendations by me at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readingwithhippos.com">www.readingwithhippos.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4655952591041880599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6014238523230760949">I should start by saying that I am not a Lindsey Stirling fan, I know about her more from <i>Dancing with the Stars</i> than from her music, but the popsugar challenge required that I read a book written by a musician and I thought I would try this as she is a member of the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints (as I am) so I did not think there would be content that would make me uncomfortable (I was right about this).   <span id="freeText6014238523230760949" style="display:none">I should start by saying that I am not a Lindsey Stirling fan, I know about her more from <i>Dancing with the Stars</i> than from her music, but the popsugar challenge required that I read a book written by a musician and I thought I would try this as she is a member of the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints (as I am) so I did not think there would be content that would make me uncomfortable (I was right about this). But, this turned out to be much more fun than I thought, Lindsey has a delightful, friendly, fun tone and has a lot of stories to tell about her short life. It was also really interesting to get some inside information about how the music business works, or at least how it has worked for her. (I will never see Andrea Bocelli in the same way again). I also really enjoyed learning about how she is trying to become the best person she can. That is what really inspires me in any person. So maybe I am a Lindsey Stirling fan after all even if I never listen to her music.<br />Popsugar 2019: A book written by a musician</span>

<div id="review_1564228620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1564228620" />
    <a title="Lorien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11389485-lorien"><img alt="Lorien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400836375p2/11389485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1564228620?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorien" href="/user/show/11389485-lorien">Lorien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11389485-lorien?shelf=personal-library">personal-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11389485-lorien?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11389485-lorien?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11389485-lorien?shelf=first-editions-first-printings">first-editions-first-printings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1564228620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3841209489888628214">Wow, I can't believe I basically read this in 2 sittings!<br/><br/>This is an autobiography of Lindsey Stirling's life, the life of someone rejected time and again, facing heartache and demons, and ultimately how she made it on YouTube. But it feels so much more.<br/><br/>As a fellow LDS girl who feels like a fish out of water, and who battles mental illness everyday (one that really does feel incurable and is much more unstable, trust me), this was beyond inspiring. Lindsey broke all the rules except for the ones </span>
  <span id="freeText3841209489888628214" style="display:none">Wow, I can't believe I basically read this in 2 sittings!<br /><br />This is an autobiography of Lindsey Stirling's life, the life of someone rejected time and again, facing heartache and demons, and ultimately how she made it on YouTube. But it feels so much more.<br /><br />As a fellow LDS girl who feels like a fish out of water, and who battles mental illness everyday (one that really does feel incurable and is much more unstable, trust me), this was beyond inspiring. Lindsey broke all the rules except for the ones that really mattered, and is doing something insane, impossible, something that many still look down on her for. And yet she's achieved incredible goals and has done so much.<br /><br />From a simple childhood staying just barely out of poverty, to struggling with a crippling mental illness that almost cost her one of the most important relationships in her life, to making it and yet still being passed over time and again, this book is super personal for her, reveling lots of secrets (such as how many times she's seen Gavi in his underwear and that she sings/screeches to make sure people don't walk in on her). It's hilarious, it broke my heart, and I absolutely recommend it. While other YouTubers and stars have down their own books, none of them could touch me quite so much. When she talked about how she felt Heavenly Father had her back even when she was falling apart, I got it. When her chapter on drinking and drug use was 1 sentence "I have never done drugs or consumed alcohol, so this chapter is really short" I found it not only hilarious but what my life looked like, except mine would be 2 sentences. "I haven't done drugs, and I sipped champagne once in my life. It was nasty and I spit it out."<br /><br />While Lindsey has spoken about how people feel that she's their friend and she's never seen them before, I really wish she was my friend. She's one of my biggest inspirations. Not just because she's a Mormon doing a job most Mormon's will never want to do, and doing it while keeping her standards high, no. And not just because she's battled mental illness and keeps fighting it everyday while trying to stay positive. It's because of all of that and so much more. Her story, how she lives her life, and of course her music helps me every day.<br /><br />I'm always saying I'm not a mega fan of anyone. Growing up super poor, and yet knowing I have a car when most of my friends didn't meant I don't take my money for granted. I can't follow anyone because it takes so much time and money and I have other things to do. But since the first time a friend shared her Zelda Medley to my Facebook, I went from fan, to big fan, to close to being a mega fan. I still can't afford one of her shirts, and I've only seen her in concert twice, but as I've only been to two concerts before, it kinda speaks loudly. I follow her everywhere I can (except on mobile stuff, my phone is crap), and try to keep up to date on her life. When Gavi died I cried, and prayed for her and his family, and I did the same when he got sick. I still worry about her.<br /><br />But I don't just recommend this book as a fan. I recommend it to everyone because the struggles are real, and when she talked about how her mental illness consumed her I got it. Mine consumes me more often than it should. I get what she means about how her anxiety keeps her from interacting, and that it's rather selfish to be that way, and yet even when you try you sometimes go to events and things and all every single person there does is look down their nose at you. (Andrea Bocelli, you're shitty. Straight up don't act like that to anyone, that makes you look like you're really a nothing inside.)<br /><br />This book is real, it's raw, and it's funny. It doesn't make you uncomfortable (trust me MOST books make me VERY uncomfortable), it has you reading it for 6 hours straight and then 2 more. I adore this book, I adore Lindsey and I know she'll continue to rise and be great. I love how she admits her faults and then does her best to continue to grow. I really need to do the same.<br /><br />5/5 stars HANDS DOWN!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3841209489888628214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1365326681" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1365326681" />
    <a title="Madeline Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24383490-madeline-rose"><img alt="Madeline Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590004042p2/24383490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1365326681?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline Rose" href="/user/show/24383490-madeline-rose">Madeline Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24383490-madeline-rose?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24383490-madeline-rose?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24383490-madeline-rose?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24383490-madeline-rose?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365326681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5173627257603992283"><b> Initial Response </b><br/>...Lindsey is awesome. <br/><br/><i>Lindsey is not afraid to be herself. In fact, it’s her confidence and individuality that have propelled her into the spotlight. But the road hasn’t been easy. After being rejected by talent scouts, music reps, and eventually national television, Lindsey forged her own path, step by step. Here, for the first time, she shares every triumph and trial she has faced until now. Beginning in a humble yet charmed childhood, this book follows Lindsey through a hum</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5173627257603992283" style="display:none"><b> Initial Response </b><br />...Lindsey is awesome. <br /><br /><i>Lindsey is not afraid to be herself. In fact, it’s her confidence and individuality that have propelled her into the spotlight. But the road hasn’t been easy. After being rejected by talent scouts, music reps, and eventually national television, Lindsey forged her own path, step by step. Here, for the first time, she shares every triumph and trial she has faced until now. Beginning in a humble yet charmed childhood, this book follows Lindsey through a humorous adolescence, to her life as a struggling musician, through her personal struggles with anorexia, and finally all the way to her success as a world-class entertainer. Lindsey’s magnetizing story is at once remarkable and universal—a testimony that there is no singular recipe for success. And a witness that, despite what people may say, sometimes it’s okay to be The Only Pirate at the Party.</i><br /><br /><b> High Lights </b><br />- I've been a HUGE fan of Lindsey Stirling ever since I watched her video <i> Elements </i>. I've been hooked ever since, and, naturally, I was really excited when her book came out.<br />- It really just reminded me that celebs are people too. (Though, she says she's not a celebrity by any means, but in my eyes she is.) She's just a normal girl who's doing what she loves. And that's a huge inspiration to me.<br />- I love the close relationship she has with her family, which you just don't see very often in business. It made me love her a ton more for that. (Her sister actually co-wrote the book with her!)<br />- I just love how much her love of music is evident. That she would go through all sorts of embarrassment and humiliation (on live TV) to pursue her dream? That's awesome.<br /><br /><b> Low Lights </b><br />- Guys, I can't say anything bad about this, honestly. It's just a great, inspiring, funny book. <br /><br /><b> Conclusion </b><br />If you're a fan of Lindsey, or even if you're not, this is a heartwarming autobiography that I think anyone trying to pursue their dream will find very encouraging. I highly recommend! <br />4/5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5173627257603992283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText12878724890915079269" style="display:none">I'm not the biggest fan of autobiographies. In fact, I usually tend to avoid them. I thought it was quite interesting to know not only the darkest moments of her life, but also how she overcame all the difficulties.
